    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer6390046098726188634">Based on the real-life adventures of Laura Ingalls Wilder, Little House in the Big Woods is the first book in the award-winning Little House series, which has captivated generations of readers. This edition features the classic black-and-white artwork from Garth Williams.<br/><br/>Little House in the Big Woods takes place in 1871 and introduces us to four-year-old Laura, who lives i</span>
  <span id="freeText6390046098726188634" style="display:none">Based on the real-life adventures of Laura Ingalls Wilder, Little House in the Big Woods is the first book in the award-winning Little House series, which has captivated generations of readers. This edition features the classic black-and-white artwork from Garth Williams.<br /><br />Little House in the Big Woods takes place in 1871 and introduces us to four-year-old Laura, who lives in a log cabin on the edge of the Big Woods of Wisconsin. She shares the cabin with her Pa, her Ma, her sisters Mary and Carrie, and their lovable dog, Jack.<br /><br />Pioneer life isn’t easy for the Ingalls family, since they must grow or catch all their own food as they get ready for the cold winter. But they make the best of every tough situation. They celebrate Christmas with homemade toys and treats, do their spring planting, bring in the harvest in the fall, and make their first trip into town. And every night, safe and warm in their little house, the sound of Pa’s fiddle lulls Laura and her sisters into sleep.<br /><br />The nine books in the timeless Little House series tell the story of Laura’s real childhood as an American pioneer, and are cherished by readers of all generations. They offer a unique glimpse into life on the American frontier, and tell the heartwarming, unforgettable story of a loving family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6390046098726188634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes and no. It's not pure autobiography, but many people lived the same way at that time. I grew up thinking it was non fiction but it's not; it's a c<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes and no. It's not pure autobiography, but many people lived the same way at that time. I grew up thinking it was non fiction but it's not; it's a composite of many people's lives.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134676967" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590488174" href="/book/show/2612801-little-house-in-the-big-woods">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134676967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17976706217982354956"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585499756i/29193446._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>Stuck at home?</b> Got some time on your hands? Want to start <b>a long series</b>? But you don't want a dud?<br/><br/>Then I have some suggestions for you!<br/><br/>Check out this<b>
  <u> <a href='https://youtu.be/Xxa4N5jdFa8' rel='nofollow noopener'>booktube video</a></u>
</b> all about which series are worth your time (and which ones aren't)! <br/><br/>Thanks for watching and happy reading!<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Check Out the Written Review!</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>You don't need magic to make a series magical</b>.<br/><br/>Four-year-old Laura Ingalls Wilder lives with her Ma, Pa and sisters, Mary & Carrie, in a little house in the big woods of Wisconsin in 1871.<br/><br/>We </span>
  <span id="freeText17976706217982354956" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585499756i/29193446._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>Stuck at home?</b> Got some time on your hands? Want to start <b>a long series</b>? But you don't want a dud?<br><br>Then I have some suggestions for you!<br><br>Check out this<b>
  <u> <a href="https://youtu.be/Xxa4N5jdFa8" rel="nofollow noopener">booktube video</a></u>
</b> all about which series are worth your time (and which ones aren't)! <br><br>Thanks for watching and happy reading!<br><br><b>
  <u>Check Out the Written Review!</u>
</b><br><br><b>You don't need magic to make a series magical</b>.<br><br>Four-year-old Laura Ingalls Wilder lives with her Ma, Pa and sisters, Mary &amp; Carrie, in a little house in the big woods of Wisconsin in 1871.<br><br>We follow a year in the life of Laura - from<b> celebrating Christmas to the fall harvest. </b><br><br>The Ingalls family is always bustling about and preparing for the next season. There very survival depends on their cooperation.<br><br> In the winter, we watch them make maple sugar, in spring they plant the garden, the summer they play in the fields and fall they gather their ccrops. <br><br>From <b>corn-husk dolls</b> to pig roasts to <b>sugaring-off parties</b> - they are busy, busy, busy. <blockquote>
  <i>The barrels of salted fish were in the pantry, and yellow cheeses were stacked on the pantry shelves. </i>
</blockquote>Despite the tough circumstances, they always make it work with <b>Ma's gentle guidance and Pa's happy fiddle</b>. <blockquote>She was glad that the cozy house, and Pa and Ma and the firelight and the music, were now. They could not be forgotten, she thought, because now is now. It can never be a long time ago. </blockquote> For a series written so long ago and geared towards young children, <b>this holds so well.</b><br><br>All the little details make this story come alive. <br><br> Every time I go back to this story, I am just as <b>enraptured and enthralled </b> as I was when I was a little girl. <br><br> All activities seem so different from the commonplace childhood memories I have...and yet, I <b>identified so closely with Laura </b> when I was younger.<br><br>I couldn't have been the only kid wishing our attic was <b>filled with preserves</b> or wanting to roast a pig tail. I'll even admit, I wanted to kick around the<b> ol' pig bladder </b> just to see what it was like.<br><br>The love, and friendship, and happiness Laura experiences along with the harsh and hungry winters truly makes for a wonderful story. <br><br>The little tales from Pa brings this book to life and Ma's gentle nurturing firmly holds together the family. Every time I read this series, I think about my own family. <b>And give my Ma and Pa a call</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>But Laura lay awake a little while, listening to Pa’s fiddle softly playing and to the lonely sound of the wind in the Big Woods.</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Narrated by Cherry Jones and accompanied on the fiddle by Paul Woodielv. Paul gave life to Pa's songs and Cherry truly made this audiobook a masterpiece. Loved every word of it.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3493105876708874568">I started rereading this series because of John Scieszka's bizarre hatred of <b>Little House on the Prairie</b>. In attempting the perfectly noble task of getting young boys to read more, Scieszka has continuously heaped scorn on that book, banishing it to the girl ghetto of the Sweet Valley High and American Girls series. Putting aside the unfair comparison to syndicate titles published for purely commercial reasons, his assesment of <b>Little House</b> as a book purely for girls is infuriating.<br/><br/>For one thing</span>
  <span id="freeText3493105876708874568" style="display:none">I started rereading this series because of John Scieszka's bizarre hatred of <b>Little House on the Prairie</b>. In attempting the perfectly noble task of getting young boys to read more, Scieszka has continuously heaped scorn on that book, banishing it to the girl ghetto of the Sweet Valley High and American Girls series. Putting aside the unfair comparison to syndicate titles published for purely commercial reasons, his assesment of <b>Little House</b> as a book purely for girls is infuriating.<br /><br />For one thing, gender-segregated reading rubs me the wrong way. For another thing, these books contain aspects that any child might enjoy. There's farming, hunting, construction, cooking, locust plagues, wolf packs, riots, blizzards, tragedy, hope, family, hard work, preserverance, horses, dogs, railroads, envy, loss, and triumph. Ignore the sugary-sweet, insipid television series - these books are genuine and engaging.</span>

<div id="review_3420644091" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3420644091" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3420644091?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060264307" href="/book/show/441602.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=young-children-s-books">young-children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=audio-companion">audio-companion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3420644091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer75025060244403239"><i>Little House in the Big Woods</i> by Laura Ingalls Wilder is a story that tells of Laura’s early childhood and upbringing in Wisconsin during the 1870s. Readers learn how her family had to live and survive in a little log cabin during pioneer times. <br/><br/>In some ways life seems much simpler during this time period, but the hard work that was necessary to survive had to be arduous. Either you grew a garden and hunted or you didn’t eat. You chopped wood or didn’t have heat for the hard, frosty winters. The</span>
  <span id="freeText75025060244403239" style="display:none"><i>Little House in the Big Woods</i> by Laura Ingalls Wilder is a story that tells of Laura’s early childhood and upbringing in Wisconsin during the 1870s. Readers learn how her family had to live and survive in a little log cabin during pioneer times. <br /><br />In some ways life seems much simpler during this time period, but the hard work that was necessary to survive had to be arduous. Either you grew a garden and hunted or you didn’t eat. You chopped wood or didn’t have heat for the hard, frosty winters. There wasn’t much entertainment available or toys to play with. Children had daily chores that had to be done. Because Laura’s family are devout Christians, Sunday’s are reserved for church and Bible and nothing else. There were strict rules. I think young readers will be fascinated comparing what life was like then to how they live now. <br /><br />This book was extremely thought-provoking to me. It conjured up thoughts from the past and present, making me think of the differences between my upbringing in the city compared to rural, country living now. When we moved over a decade ago I had visions of becoming a homesteader, until I was thrust into the harsh realities of raising animals for food. I learned really quick that I lacked something others around me didn’t: the capability to kill an animal that you nurtured and cared for. My first visit to the backyard butcher was like culture shock. That day my distant neighbor (who’s a homesteader) made the comment that my generation will never survive. Obviously when it comes down to survival, people will do what they have to, in contrast to our day and age now where it’s so convenient to just head to the supermarket and grab some meat that someone else processed, or produce someone else grew. In this book they’re hunting mainly wild deer, but they do have pigs that the children care for. The story gets quite graphic—sharing the preparation of the meat after hunting. Obviously I’m not a hunter either, but what if it came down to surviving and the need to feed my family without farmers? These are just some of the thoughts that came to mind when reading this with my children. <br /><br />Overall, we enjoyed this story and have plans to finish the entire series. I always admire themes of family and kindness, and the love this family shares is something special. Times spent singing and listening to Pa’s fiddle by the fire were my favorites. The children do find ways to have fun during their chores which is nice. It’s such a cozy tale at times, written well with beautiful descriptions, and one we’ll likely revisit in the future. <br /><br />If you’re reading this with children, I highly recommend the audio companion to the book by Cherry Jones. We used it along with the physical books. Cherry does a wonderful job with the audio and even sings along. It really brings the story to life.<br /><br />4****</span>
  <a data-text-id="75025060244403239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2076230408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2076230408" />
    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2076230408?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060581800" href="/book/show/1212387.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=childhood-favorites">childhood-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076230408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7863881036465534385">My two younger daughters recently discovered the Little House series and are speeding through the books this summer. As I am in between books and wanted to avoid a reading rut, I decided to revisit the first book in the series for myself. As I am always on the lookout for quality children's books, I spent a few hours rereading the beginning of a series that I had enjoyed when I was my daughters' age. <br/><br/>Little House in the Big Woods begins the classic children's saga that follows Laura Ingalls Wild</span>
  <span id="freeText7863881036465534385" style="display:none">My two younger daughters recently discovered the Little House series and are speeding through the books this summer. As I am in between books and wanted to avoid a reading rut, I decided to revisit the first book in the series for myself. As I am always on the lookout for quality children's books, I spent a few hours rereading the beginning of a series that I had enjoyed when I was my daughters' age. <br /><br />Little House in the Big Woods begins the classic children's saga that follows Laura Ingalls Wilder on her journey from childhood to marriage. It features a wide eyed five year old girl who has her entire future ahead of her at a thrilling time in American history as the country has moved past the civil war and is starting to settle the west. Ingalls was born in 1867 in the big woods of Wisconsin. She lives with her parents and sisters Mary and Carrie in a log cabin in the middle of the woods and has rarely traveled anywhere other than to visit her grandparents and aunts, uncles, and cousins. The woods and all that was in it made up her entire life. <br /><br />Even if the country was beginning to modernize, and we glimpse it with the horse powered threshing machine toward the end, the industrial revolution had yet to come to Wisconsin. The Ingalls family lived according to the seasons of the year, was a devout Christian family, and each member of the family worked from morning to night doing their share of chores. Pa hunted and farmed while Ma cooked, baked, and sewed the entire family's clothing from scratch. Mary and Laura were expected to do their share of chores as well, including helping with the dishes and basic needlepoint and cross stitch. Both girls were model citizens who children of today could learn many lessons from, especially in obeying their parents and knowing to be seen and not heard. <br /><br />The edition I read is the collectors edition illustrated by Garth Williams. Williams had illustrated over one hundred books for children including the classic Charlotte's Web. His illustrations bring Laura's life to life as readers see her dancing at her grandpa's barn dance, going into town, and her daily life throughout the year. Williams met an adult Ingalls and traveled to all of her homes in order to view first hand how she lived. I felt the illustrations were vital as children are reading about a different era in history, and illustrations can assist them on their journey through time. Even an adult can benefit from viewing color illustrations as they can once again become captivated by a series they read as children. <br /><br />As an elementary aged student, my favorite series was All of a Kind Family. I had much in common with the girls in the story and reread more times than I could count. Yet, Little House was easily a close second as I was and am a lover of history and enjoyed reading about a girl and her family in an earlier part of my nation's history. I am glad my daughters have discovered this series as we can share our memories of it as they continue Laura and her family's journey through life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7863881036465534385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3458729071?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060264314" href="/book/show/1212409.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=read-with-kids">read-with-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3458729071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3544205792995800533">Another classic read with the kids!<br/><br/>I think as we get more into an era where kids don’t know a time without computers and easily accessible technology, books like Little House in the Big Woods will start to appeal less to the young crowd. Listening to stories of pioneer life is so far removed from what they know it is at times incomprehensible. At least when I was a kid we were not all that far removed from a simpler and less wired lifestyle. I do think my kids enjoyed the time we took to read th</span>
  <span id="freeText3544205792995800533" style="display:none">Another classic read with the kids!<br /><br />I think as we get more into an era where kids don’t know a time without computers and easily accessible technology, books like Little House in the Big Woods will start to appeal less to the young crowd. Listening to stories of pioneer life is so far removed from what they know it is at times incomprehensible. At least when I was a kid we were not all that far removed from a simpler and less wired lifestyle. I do think my kids enjoyed the time we took to read this together, but it was much less easier for them to stay interested in than in some other books we read (Willy Wonka and his fantastic factory and elevator, Bunnicula the vampire rabbit, Ralph and his Motorcycle (which also had some more old timey content that was a bit hard to connect to, but nothing like Little House)). I will continue to read to them and hope to keep the spirit of these classics alive.<br /><br />I know that this was the second time reading this. I vividly remember the cover as the same one from elementary school. But before I re-read it, it would have been impossible for me to tell you anything about it. However, as our family got into it, I noticed some of the parts were very familiar. Apparently, I had retained a lot of the content, but my brain hadn’t filed it with any point of reference. I kept looking at my wife and kids while I was reading and saying, “Hey, I remember this!”<br /><br />But I am also pretty sure that this is the only book I read in the series. I never moved on to Little House on the Prairie and I never watched the television show. Maybe this time I will move on to the second book with my family. Seems like I really must at some point to get the full feel of this classic series.<br /><br />One major thing to point out about the first book that stood out to me, and is not really a criticism - it just is what it is – is that there is not a whole lot of plot. The point of the book is that each chapter shares a little bit of what life was like for the children while living through the year secluded in the big woods. So, instead of a beginning, middle, and end, you get a series of detailed anecdotes about some aspect of life in the cabin. I would be interested to know if that is how the rest of the series is as well.<br /><br />This selection is worth checking out – especially if you are looking for something easy to read with the kids.<br /><br />Disclaimer: Frequently as of late, books and movies have been putting disclaimers on content with dated cultural depictions. While Little House in the Big Woods does seem sweet and innocent, there is a song sung by the father with racial slurs. I am sure it was representative of what was acceptable at the time, but I wanted to make sure that anyone who might be sensitive to this know about it up front.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3544205792995800533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11316635252384892294">I grew up with the <i>Little House on the Prairie</i> tv series, but I didn't read any of the actual books until my son was about seven. We read all nine books together, and before we knew what was happening, I was wearing a bonnet and we'd traveled to all of the Laura Ingalls Wilder historic sites in South Dakota, Minnesota and Missouri. <br/><br/>(I can only bless my son for his patience and grace that hot summer day as he stood politely over by a tree while I had an animated conversation and shared some hot t</span>
  <span id="freeText11316635252384892294" style="display:none">I grew up with the <i>Little House on the Prairie</i> tv series, but I didn't read any of the actual books until my son was about seven. We read all nine books together, and before we knew what was happening, I was wearing a bonnet and we'd traveled to all of the Laura Ingalls Wilder historic sites in South Dakota, Minnesota and Missouri. <br><br>(I can only bless my son for his patience and grace that hot summer day as he stood politely over by a tree while I had an animated conversation and shared some hot tears with Laura, at her grave in Mansfield, Missouri).<br><br>When I read the series to my middle child, she'd already seen the photos of her mother's and brother's Laura Ingalls adventures, and she was ready to don the bonnet and aprons, but I told her she needed to wait until her little sister had experienced the books and then we'd go together, as a family.<br><br>This past week marked my youngest child's first exposure to the series, (this book being the perfect selection, also, for our “Wisconsin” entry of our Kids Read Across America project).<br><br>To be honest, I didn't know how this particular reading experience was going to go. This child, my third child, is my “Janis Joplin.” She moves around quite a bit while I'm reading to her, often humming or singing under her breath, and she's the most challenging of my kids to engage.<br><br>For the first several chapters of this book, she kept saying, “So that girl with the brown hair. She's telling the story?” When I explained that yes, this is Laura's story, and it's a true story, she would say, “So, she's still a girl?” When I explained that no, she's not a girl anymore, and she is in fact dead now, my daughter became horrified, and wondered how a dead woman wrote this story. <br><br>I'm not sure why we got stuck in this loop, but we did. For a couple of nights.<br><br>Eventually, the story completely took over her senses and she absolutely loved it. Loved it so much in fact, she demanded to know when we were going to “Laura's house,” like Ryan did when he was little. She also said she doesn't want to read any more states in our challenge, she just wants to read this series. <br><br>Wow. Can you believe, after all of these years, that this story of pioneer life in the 1870s is still so engaging to a modern child (even despite the descriptions of Pa hunting and slaughtering animals for dinner?)<br><br>This will be my favorite memory of reading this classic to my youngest child. . . when we got to the part where little Laura is sitting with her sister, Mary, there's this charming illustration of the sisters with their dolls:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600203051i/30111260.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I pointed out to my daughter that Mary had a rag doll made by her mother, but Laura had only a corncob for a doll. I explained “that's how things were, back then. Children didn't have as many things as you have now.”<br><br>I think my daughter was chomping on a big wad of gum at this moment, and she pointed at the corncob doll and said, “That? That piece of corn was her doll?”<br>I said, “Yep. Can you imagine that being all you had?”<br><br>She shook her head and said, “Damn.”<br><br>I looked at her and said, “<i>Damn?</i> That's adult language, honey. Where did you learn that word?”<br><br>She said, “The other day, Mommy, you said to Daddy: I can't get anything on this damn computer to work.”<br><br>Sigh. <br>Ma and Pa would be so proud, wouldn't they??<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600203051i/30111261.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11316635252384892294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1865542530252360415">The Little House on the Prairie books bring back so many good memories. I have been looking for my box of old books for awhile now but still haven't found it. I'm really hoping it didn't get lost when I moved last year. There are so many books that I would love to re-read. <br/><br/>I'm not sure why I didn't read these to my daughter. I think she had so many books that we just never got around to it. <br/><br/>Little House in the Big Woods is the first book of the series and will always be my favorite, but I did en</span>
  <span id="freeText1865542530252360415" style="display:none">The Little House on the Prairie books bring back so many good memories. I have been looking for my box of old books for awhile now but still haven't found it. I'm really hoping it didn't get lost when I moved last year. There are so many books that I would love to re-read. <br /><br />I'm not sure why I didn't read these to my daughter. I think she had so many books that we just never got around to it. <br /><br />Little House in the Big Woods is the first book of the series and will always be my favorite, but I did enjoy all of the books in the collection. I tried to find the edition on here that looked most like what I remember, and I think this is the same cover that was on my book. <br /><br />I can clearly my mom reading it to me before I could read myself. Sitting on my bed next to her watching as she read. Once I was able to read it myself I picked it up again to read to her, watching as her fingers slid underneath the words and helping me with the hard ones. She mentioned the other day that it's one of her favorite memories too. <br /><br />I loved all of the characters. Laura, Ma, Pa, Carrie and Mary as well as many others. I dreamt of living in that little cabin in the woods and desperately wanted Laura Ingalls as a best friend. The fun and adventures these children had along with their dog, Jack was entertaining every time it was read to me or by me. <br /><br />When it was turned into a TV show, I was escastic! I remember it was on every Sunday at 6pm on Channel 2. I was allowed to watch it while sitting in my dads lazy-boy recliner and nothing could tear me away. <br /><br />If I can't find my old books I will definitley buy another collection as I would love to re-read them at some point. <br /><br />Even writing this review has brought back great memories of these wonderful stories &lt;3<br /><br /></span>

    <a title="Duane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24389390-duane"><img alt="Duane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403316391p2/24389390.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1427365663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17494358866205888025">This is the first book in the Little House Series, and somewhat overlooked due to the popularity of the second book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77767.Little_House_on_the_Prairie__Little_House___2_' title='Little House on the Prairie (Little House, #2) by Laura Ingalls Wilder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little House on the Prairie</a>. I've read both and liked both; this volume being a wonderful introduction to Laura and the Ingalls familly. I didn't read this series as a child, but as an adult I've come to appreciate it's beauty, and it's importance in the canon of American Children's Literature. Some may say this is too simple for adults to appreciate, and starting out it seems tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17494358866205888025" style="display:none">This is the first book in the Little House Series, and somewhat overlooked due to the popularity of the second book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77767.Little_House_on_the_Prairie__Little_House___2_" title="Little House on the Prairie (Little House, #2) by Laura Ingalls Wilder" rel="nofollow noopener">Little House on the Prairie</a>. I've read both and liked both; this volume being a wonderful introduction to Laura and the Ingalls familly. I didn't read this series as a child, but as an adult I've come to appreciate it's beauty, and it's importance in the canon of American Children's Literature. Some may say this is too simple for adults to appreciate, and starting out it seems that way, but the more you read the more you realize that Ingall's style is perfect for this type of story. I'm glad I started the series and I look forward to reading more.<br /><br />Revised January 2018.</span>

This series should be on the reading list for every mother.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1746285348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1746285348" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1746285348?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780064400015" href="/book/show/77766.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">stealth libertarians</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746285348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12758383405103650044"><i>Little House in the Big Woods</i> is what <i>Walden</i> wishes it was, or could have been if Thoreau wasn't <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015650683' title='My review' rel='nofollow noopener'>such a dick.</a> Laura and her family aren't misanthropic creeps - and they have real skills, unlike vacationing Thoreau. But the book is about self-reliance, getting back to the basics, and living in harmony with nature. It shares a philosophy with <i>Walden</i> - along with two other sortof less-great things.<br/><br/>The first is a hopeless lack of plot, and that frustrated me when I first read it. And I do mean <i>first</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12758383405103650044" style="display:none"><i>Little House in the Big Woods</i> is what <i>Walden</i> wishes it was, or could have been if Thoreau wasn't <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015650683" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">such a dick.</a> Laura and her family aren't misanthropic creeps - and they have real skills, unlike vacationing Thoreau. But the book is about self-reliance, getting back to the basics, and living in harmony with nature. It shares a philosophy with <i>Walden</i> - along with two other sortof less-great things.<br /><br />The first is a hopeless lack of plot, and that frustrated me when I first read it. And I do mean <i>first read:</i> this was the first chapter book I ever read all by myself. I battled through the entire series, because my mother told me I'd be a good reader when I was done, and I suppose it worked (I can read!) but honestly I should have just stuck to comic books; the meandering pace here wasn't a great match for little me. (Some of the <i>Little House</i> books have more plot than others.)<br /><br />The second thing <i>Little House</i> shares with <i>Walden</i> is that it's <a href="https://www.bostonglobe.com/ideas/2013/08/09/little-libertarians-prairie-little-libertarians-prairie/DrtramwsrcrdTTIFvdzkOO/story.html" title="Great, lengthy Boston Globe article with more on everything I say here" rel="nofollow noopener">bullshit.</a> Thoreau went home to his mommy when he wanted cookies, and Laura's real life family were subsistence farmers always one bad season away from starving to death. Wilder leaves out her real brother's death in infancy to focus on singing by the fire. Both books hide the hardships of the lives they promote.<br /><br />Wilder's book was published in 1932, during the Depression, and it was a collaboration between Wilder and her daughter Rose Wilder Lane, who was a successful novelist and also a rabid libertarian who advocated the assassination of New Dealing FDR and threatened to <a href="http://www.newyorker.com/books/page-turner/a-libertarian-house-on-the-prairie" title="New Yorker article with almost exactly the same title as the Globe one" rel="nofollow noopener">do it herself.</a> This is the story Lane and Wilder want to sell you: hardy stock living by their own hard work without government interference. In reality, the Wilders lived harsh and desperate lives. Young, just-married Laura's first farm failed, and she lost it. It was only these books that finally pulled her out of a life of poverty - these books, which advocated exactly the grueling life they rescued her from.<br /><br />That said, this is still a great source of information about such topics as:<br />- Making maple sugar<br />- Square dancing<br />- How much Laura's sister sucks<br />- Why children should be seen and not heard - remember when that was a thing? Ha!<br />- Old-timey songs, and there's a song about an "old darkey" who dies that you will need to watch out for if you're reading this to your child. It's in chapter 5. That's the only truly oh-shit content.<br />- Weaving straw hats<br />- Old-time candy - if there is a plot, it's that Laura Ingalls Wilder has a sweet tooth; this book is basically about candy<br />- Leaving babies in a pile on a bed while everyone does square dancing<br />- Extremely specific gender roles<br /><br />It's pleasant enough to read, if a little boring. Just keep in mind, when Laura says,<blockquote>"This is now." <br /><br />She was glad that the cosy house, and Pa and Ma and the firelight and the music, were now. They could not be forgotten, she thought, because now is now. It can never be a long time ago.</blockquote><br />It can never be now, either; it never existed at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12758383405103650044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383857164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11817092588507693187">For a few years now, I've been interviewing my twins after they finish reading their books, posting those interviews on their own <i>goodreads</i> profile. My girl, Brontë, finished reading Little House in the Big Woods about a month ago, and I read it this week (I always read or reread the books they've read.) You can see that interview with me right here:<br/><br/>Brontë: So first ... did you like it? did you love it? or did you hate? did you think it was okay? or did you really like it?<br/><br/>Pa: I loved it. It was </span>
  <span id="freeText11817092588507693187" style="display:none">For a few years now, I've been interviewing my twins after they finish reading their books, posting those interviews on their own <i>goodreads</i> profile. My girl, Brontë, finished reading Little House in the Big Woods about a month ago, and I read it this week (I always read or reread the books they've read.) You can see that interview with me right here:<br /><br />Brontë: So first ... did you like it? did you love it? or did you hate? did you think it was okay? or did you really like it?<br /><br />Pa: I loved it. It was good. Much better than I expected. <br /><br />Brontë: Who was your favourite character?<br /><br />Pa: Hmmm ... that's a tough one because I loved Pa and Laura a lot, but I also dug Ma. Mary's a bit of pain, but to be fair, the story is being told by Laura, and little sisters don't tend to be too kind to their older sisters. So maybe I can't judge Mary on that. But I guess I like Pa the best because he's really the focus of the story for Laura. He's the one she talks most about. And he seems like a pretty good guy.<br /><br />Brontë: Interesting. <br /><br />Pa: Did you expect something different? Did you think I'd like someone else?<br /><br />Brontë: I thought you'd say Laura, but my second favourite was Pa. <br /><br />Pa: So we're reversed.<br /><br />Brontë: Yeah. <br /><br />Pa: I figured you'd like Laura best. <br /><br />Brontë: What was your favourite moment and your favourite chapter?<br /><br />Pa: My favourite moment was when Ma slapped the bear in the night. That was awesome. And my favourite chapter was the Maple Syrup dance on the day of the sugar snow. That was pretty cool. I loved how everyone really just had fun even with all the hard work that still had to be done. <br /><br />Brontë: Did you like the Harvest chapter?<br /><br />Pa: That must have been your favourite.<br /><br />Brontë: It was one of my favourites.<br /><br />Pa: Yeah. I liked it. It was awesome. Charley deserved to get stung by the bees.<br /><br />Brontë: Yeah he did. When that happened I almost said, "Get off your lazy butt and do some work!" <br /><br />Pa: Yeah he was lazy all right, and a total pain the ass. Pa didn't approve of the way Charley ignored his Dad, did he?<br /><br />Brontë: No, he didn't. I thought the same thing. I love how in the picture when he was wrapped in the bandages all the girls were staring at him with mean faces on. <br /><br />Pa: That's something else I loved, the art.<br /><br />Brontë: Oh yeah, the art was beautiful.<br /><br />Pa: But Laura's writing was even more beautiful. I was impressed. <br /><br />Brontë: I agree.<br /><br />Pa: It was so clear and descriptive, and I felt like I was there sometimes. <br /><br />Brontë: Me too. Every moment I felt like I watched it in my head. <br /><br />Pa: It's cool when you read a book like that.<br /><br />Brontë: And then I could look at the pictures and think, that's what the boys and girls look like and watch it in my head as I read. <br /><br />Pa: I think I could see what they looked like even without the pictures. <br /><br />Brontë: Yeah, me too. <br /><br />Pa: The writing was just that good. <br /><br />Brontë: Especially what she said, like in the dance part when the girls were getting ready, and she described what the dresses looked like and you could totally see the dresses in your head. <br /><br />Pa: Darn good book. Thanks for reading it so I could.<br /><br />Brontë: No problem. Don't forget to say thanks to Auntie Marci too.<br /><br />Pa: And Ma. It's her book.<br /><br />Brontë: Yeah, you're right. <br /><br />Pa: So when are you going to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77767.Little_House_on_the_Prairie" title="Little House on the Prairie by Laura Ingalls Wilder" rel="nofollow noopener">Little House on the Prairie</a>?<br /><br />Brontë: Umm ... after I finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12630577.The_Templeton_Twins_Have_an_Idea" title="The Templeton Twins Have an Idea by Ellis Weiner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Templeton Twins</a>.<br /><br />Pa: I'm looking forward to it.</span>

  <span id="freeText674181103948982838" style="display:none">I was obsessed with the Litte House books and the TV show when I was a child. <span id="freeTextContainer8150954663742333361">Little House in the Big Woods (Little House #1), Laura Ingalls Wilder<br/>Laura Ingall’s story begins in 1871 in a little log cabin on the edge of the Big Woods of Wisconsin. Four-year-old Laura lives in the little house with her Pa, her Ma, her sisters Mary and Carrie, and their trusty dog, Jack. Pioneer life is sometimes hard, since the family must grow or catch all their own food as they get ready for the cold winter. But it is also exciting as Laura and her folks celebrate Christmas with homemade</span>
  <span id="freeText8150954663742333361" style="display:none">Little House in the Big Woods (Little House #1), Laura Ingalls Wilder<br />Laura Ingall’s story begins in 1871 in a little log cabin on the edge of the Big Woods of Wisconsin. Four-year-old Laura lives in the little house with her Pa, her Ma, her sisters Mary and Carrie, and their trusty dog, Jack. Pioneer life is sometimes hard, since the family must grow or catch all their own food as they get ready for the cold winter. But it is also exciting as Laura and her folks celebrate Christmas with homemade toys and treats, do the spring planting, bring in the harvest, and make their first trip to town. And every night they are safe and warm in their little house, with the happy sound of Pa’s fiddle sending Laura and her sisters off to sleep. And so begins Laura Ingalls Wilder’s beloved story of a pioneer girl and her family. The nine Little House books have been cherished by generations of readers as both a unique glimpse into America’s frontier past and a heartwarming, unforgettable story. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1994 میلادی<br />عنوان: ک‍ل‍ب‍ه‌ ی‌ ک‍وچ‍ک‌ در ج‍ن‍گ‍ل‌ ب‍زرگ‌؛ نویسنده: ل‍ورا ای‍ن‍گ‍ال‍ز وای‍ل‍در‏‫؛ مت‍رج‍م: ک‍اظم‌ ف‍ائ‍ق‍ی‌؛ ت‍ب‍ری‍ز: ی‍اران‌‏‫، 1370؛ در 96 ص؛ موضوع: یادمانهای نویسندگان ایلات متحده امریکا - سده 20 م‬<br /><br />سری کتابهای نه گانه «خانه ی کوچک»، اثر «لورا اینگالز ویلدر»؛ دست نوشته های نویسنده، از دوران کودکی خویش است، که خوانشگران بسیاری را شیفته ی یادمانها و قلم خودش کرده است، این مجموعه داستانهایی از یک خانواده آمریکایی گرم و مهربان است<br />کتاب نخست، با عنوان: «خانه کوچک در جنگل بزرگ»: با خانواده انگالز ملاقاتی داشته باشید. مامان، بابا، مری و کری کوچولو، که همه ساکن کلبه ای نقلی در جنگل، در دهه 70 سده ی نوزدهم میلادی هستند. با اینکه همسایگان آنها: گرگها، پلنگها و خرسها هستند، جنگل برایشان همانند خانه است، چرا که دستپخت مامان و صدای ویولن پدر را دارند.؛<br />کتاب دوم با عنوان: «پسر کشاورز»؛ زمان میگذرد و لورا در خانه ی کوچک در کانزاس بزرگ میشود. آلمونزو ویلدر در مزرعه ای بزرگ در نیویورک زندگی میکند. او و برادرانش و خواهرش از سپیده دم تا وقت شام به سختی کار میکنند تا مزرعه خانوادگی را سرپا نگه دارند. آلمانزو آرزو دارد که اسبی برای خود داشته باشد، اما اول باید ثابت کند که لایق این مسئولیت بزرگ است.؛<br />کتاب سوم، با عنوان: «خانه ای کوچک در چمنزار»، وقتی پدر تصمیم میگیرد کلبه خانواده را در جنگل بفروشد، خانواده به کانزاس نقل مکان میکند، جاییکه پدر خانه ای کوچک در چمنزار برایشان ساخته است. زندگی در چمنزار با جنگل متفاوت است ولی لورا و خانواده اش خود را با زندگی جدیدشان سرگرم و شاد میکنند.؛<br />کتاب چهارم، با عنوان: «کناره های نهر آلو»؛ خانواده ی اینگالز در کنار نهر آلو در خانه ای کاهی زندگی میکنند تا پدر برایشان خانه ای مقاوم و چوبی بسازد. پول ساخت این خانه از اولین محصول گندمشان بدست خواهد آمد، اما دقیقاً فصل برداشت محصول ابرهای سیاهی آسمان را تیره کردند. میلیونها ملخ به مزرعه حمله کرده و در پایان هفته دیگر گندمی برای برداشت وجود نداشت.؛<br />کتاب پنجم با عنوان: «کنار برکه ی نقره ای»؛ پدر به بیابانی در غرب داکوتا رفت. وقتی که مادر، مری، لورا، کری و گریس کوچولو به او ملحق شدند، تبدیل به اولین ساکنین شهرک اسمت بودند. پدر مشغول ساخت اولین خانه ی این شهرک که کناره ی برکه ی نقره ای قرار داشت، شد.؛<br />کتاب ششم، با عنوان: «زمستان بلند»؛ نخستین طوفان در ماه اکتبر به چمنزار بارن آمد. سپس تا ماه آپریل، برف بدون توقف بارید. وقتی ارتفاع برف تا سقف خانه های شهرک رسید، دیگر برای قطارها ممکن نبود که به مردم شهرک محصولات برسانند. لورا، خانواده اش و مردم شهر در حال تلف شدن از گرسنگی بودند اما آلمانزو جوان که در شهر ساکن بود جان خود را برای نجات مردم به خطر میاندازد.؛<br />کتاب هفتم، با عنوان: «شهری کوچک در چمنزار (سبزه زار)»؛ بهار آمد و شهرک اسمت روحی تازه به خود گرفت. اما در کنار مهمانیها و تعطیلات، کار باید ادامه میداشت. لورا با بافتن پیراهن به پدر و مادر برای کسب درآمد کمک میکرد تا بتوانند مری را به دانشگاه نابینایان بفرستند. ولی در عصرها، لورا زمانی را برای آلمانزو ویلدر کنار میگذاشت.؛<br />کتاب هشتم، با عنوان: «این سال های طلائی»؛ لورا باید به کسب درآمد ادامه میداد تا بتواند به تحصیل مری در دانشگاه نابینایان یاری کند. به این منظور شغلی به عنوان آموزگار پیدا کرد. ساده نبود چرا که برای نخستین بار او باید دور از خانواده زندگی میکرد. ولی هر جمعه کمی زندگیش ساده تر میشد چرا که آلمانزو او را به خانه میرساند. با اینکه او بسیار جوان بود ولی میدانست که باید منتظر شروعی جدید با آلمانزو باشد.؛<br />کتاب نهم، با عنوان: «چهار سال ابتدایی»؛ لورا اینگالز و آلمانزو ویلدر به تازگی ازدواج کرده بودند. آنها به چمنزاری کوچک نقل مکان کردند تا با یکدیگر زندگی جدیدی را آغاز کنند. اما هر سال چالشی جدید در انتظارشان بود. از طوفان، آتشسوزی گرفته تا مریضی و بدهیهای بسیار. این چهار سال ابتدایی شجاعت، قدرت و مصمم بودن را میطلبید. اما با این همه ی مشکل لورا و آلمانزو عشقشان پایدار بود و با ورود رز کوچولو به زندگیشان عشقشان چند برابر هم شد. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="8150954663742333361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7190580662112271536">"Mary was bigger than Laura, and she had a rag doll named Nettie. Laura had only a corncob wrapped in a handkerchief, but it was a good doll. It was named Susan. It wasn't Susan't fault that she was only a corncob. Sometimes Mary let Laura hold Nettie, but she did it only when Susan couldn't see."<br/><br/>Came across this book, probably after more than 20 years since I read it first, and couldn't help but re-reading it again. Back then, this used to be my favorite book, and I remember reading it so many </span>
  <span id="freeText7190580662112271536" style="display:none">"Mary was bigger than Laura, and she had a rag doll named Nettie. Laura had only a corncob wrapped in a handkerchief, but it was a good doll. It was named Susan. It wasn't Susan't fault that she was only a corncob. Sometimes Mary let Laura hold Nettie, but she did it only when Susan couldn't see."<br /><br />Came across this book, probably after more than 20 years since I read it first, and couldn't help but re-reading it again. Back then, this used to be my favorite book, and I remember reading it so many times over and over. Now, though it is a very short book, I still enjoyed it, and got to relive that original feeling to some extent, taking me back to those wonderful times. I believe, anyone who had read this when they were little could easily relate to what I'm saying. Laura was, is and will be one of my all time favorite fictional characters.<br /><br />It's harder to pinpoint what exactly makes this so beautiful. May be it's the cozy little house, or lovely little family, or may be just how the Author manages to put it all together. Matters little to me that it's a children's book - for me, this has no age limit.<br /><br />"But it had been a wonderful day, the most wonderful day in her whole life. She thought about the beautiful lake, and the town she had seen, and the big store full of so many things. She held the pebbles carefully in her lap, and her candy heart wrapped carefully in her handkerchief until she got home and could put it away to keep always. It was too pretty to eat."</span>

<div id="review_562204297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/562204297" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17957823-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597778686p2/17957823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/562204297?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590488174" href="/book/show/2612801-little-house-in-the-big-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17957823-erin?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562204297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10837955154887705677">A walk down memory lane. Although I have a whole bunch of new books to read, I felt like grabbing a childhood favorite from my stacks tonight. The first book in the "Little House" series introduces readers to Laura Ingalls, her Ma &Pa, and sisters, Mary and Carrie living in their log home in the "big woods" of Wisconsin. <br/><br/>The thirteen chapters in this book serve as vignettes of what life was like for settler families, the roles and responsibilities of each family member, the customs and teachings</span>
  <span id="freeText10837955154887705677" style="display:none">A walk down memory lane. Although I have a whole bunch of new books to read, I felt like grabbing a childhood favorite from my stacks tonight. The first book in the "Little House" series introduces readers to Laura Ingalls, her Ma &amp;Pa, and sisters, Mary and Carrie living in their log home in the "big woods" of Wisconsin. <br /><br />The thirteen chapters in this book serve as vignettes of what life was like for settler families, the roles and responsibilities of each family member, the customs and teachings that had such an impact on a little girl and shape her to be a grown woman. I always felt a connection to Laura Ingalls right down to her brown hair. Intertwined with these chapters are stories of several family members misadventures that provide chuckles and lessons from beginning to end. <br /><br />It would be terrible for me to overlook the wonderful illustrations from Garth Williams that accompany the author's text. I dare say that without them as child of 9 (the age of my "discovery "), the story might not have had as much impact. <br /><br />I would definitely recommend to the young and young at heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10837955154887705677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3461186060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3461186060" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3461186060?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HBalikov" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HBalikov" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov">HBalikov</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3461186060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5900985588761372525">This is the first of the series of stories of a pioneer family that takes them to many different locations in America’s Heartland. In the Wisconsin “Big Woods” we meet Pa and Ma and young girls, Mary, Laura and baby Carrie. <br/><br/>The book covers about four seasons of experience during the last quarter of the 19th century, and we also get to meet the extended family of grandparents, uncles, aunts and cousins that the family will leave behind in the future. <br/><br/>Plenty of time is taken on description of clot</span>
  <span id="freeText5900985588761372525" style="display:none">This is the first of the series of stories of a pioneer family that takes them to many different locations in America’s Heartland. In the Wisconsin “Big Woods” we meet Pa and Ma and young girls, Mary, Laura and baby Carrie. <br /><br />The book covers about four seasons of experience during the last quarter of the 19th century, and we also get to meet the extended family of grandparents, uncles, aunts and cousins that the family will leave behind in the future. <br /><br />Plenty of time is taken on description of clothing, skills of both parents, animals (both wild and domesticated) and celebrations. We experience the family’s Christmas with expectations quite different from current times. We learn about how maple trees are tapped for what becomes syrup and confections. There are celebrations and stories about how hard/strict life was for previous generations.<br /><br />Our soon-to-be six year old was interested in most of it (though she didn’t question the unfamiliar words and we sometimes chose to add further explanation). She liked the play among the children, was a bit scared about the bee stings, wanted to hear more about maple sugar sweets and seemed to follow the plot without too much trouble. Reading this again was a different kind of pleasure – both fresh and informed by experiences since the last time decades ago.<br /><br />A fine start for the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5900985588761372525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2021823842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021823842" />
    <a title="Theresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26823570-theresa"><img alt="Theresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494367054p2/26823570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021823842?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa" href="/user/show/26823570-theresa">Theresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780064400015" href="/book/show/77766.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021823842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15485657184855930839">I wish I had read this when I was younger, because I probably would have enjoyed it more. In third grade, we were all told to read these books, but Harry Potter had just come out. Obviously, dragons and magic were more interesting than life in the Midwest, much to my teacher and my parents dismay. But back to Laura Ingalls...<br/><br/>This book is perfect for teaching any child what life was like in the late 1800's, living in the woods trying to survive. Now, it seems utterly preposterous to live this way</span>
  <span id="freeText15485657184855930839" style="display:none">I wish I had read this when I was younger, because I probably would have enjoyed it more. In third grade, we were all told to read these books, but Harry Potter had just come out. Obviously, dragons and magic were more interesting than life in the Midwest, much to my teacher and my parents dismay. But back to Laura Ingalls...<br /><br />This book is perfect for teaching any child what life was like in the late 1800's, living in the woods trying to survive. Now, it seems utterly preposterous to live this way, but I think children would benefit from this. Rules and chores were all apart of the daily routine, and the most simplest of things were entertaining to young children. They didn't have TV or video games, they went outside and played with whatever they could find...even a pig's bladder.<br /><br />My main problem with this story is there is no beginning, middle or end. There is no "plot" really, and you really could have read any chapter at any time in any order. I know it's a children's book, but I read plenty of children's books that had a plot. Even Amelia Bedelia had a plot. Life in the big woods is great, but I needed something a bit more to the story.<br /><br />I truly expected to fly through this one, but it dragged on a bit too much for me. I think its charm didn't work on me like it did for every other little girl in my third grade class.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15485657184855930839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590488174" href="/book/show/2612801-little-house-in-the-big-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=childhood-favorites">childhood-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892252522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093940771254452968">This might be my favorite book of all time. It's certainly one of the first I remember reading as a child, and it's always been an enormous source of comfort. I tried to find the other edition I have (I've got the first edition minus its dust jacket, along with the paperback set of the series), but no luck on here unfortunately. I treasure all of my books, and the Little House/Rocky Ridge series(es) in particular, but this may be the best of them. This is the one where I find myself quoting as I</span>
  <span id="freeText17093940771254452968" style="display:none">This might be my favorite book of all time. It's certainly one of the first I remember reading as a child, and it's always been an enormous source of comfort. I tried to find the other edition I have (I've got the first edition minus its dust jacket, along with the paperback set of the series), but no luck on here unfortunately. I treasure all of my books, and the Little House/Rocky Ridge series(es) in particular, but this may be the best of them. This is the one where I find myself quoting as I read, because lines have stuck with me for the last twenty-ish years. I read it in one sitting today and was so pleased to find it's lost none of its magic.<br /><br />Now I'm off to eBay to track down Laura's actual autobiography and plan a trip to Missouri and South Dakota. :D</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/5096743-suzanne">Suzanne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5096743-suzanne?shelf=children">children</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834551391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5385158325749795254">It just isn't possible for me to be objective about the Little House books. They were THE go to books for me as a child, and the comfort books as a teenager. This one is certainly written at a younger level, but I still loved reading about all of the work it took to run a farm - from making butter and cheese and straw hats, etc. Boy do I take a lot for granted. Anyway, I enjoyed it yet again! Perfect finals week comfort-reading :)<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2427440123" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2427440123" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2427440123?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590488174" href="/book/show/2612801-little-house-in-the-big-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=classics-i-ve-read">classics-i-ve-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2427440123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11786312075943710307">In the past few months, I’ve developed a bit of an obsession with the television show Little House on the Prairie. It’s something I’ve seen bits and pieces of throughout my life, as there were always reruns playing on some channel. But I’ve never sat down and watched it from the beginning as I’m doing now, and I’ve really been enjoying it. I just had a desperate desire for something pure and wholesome that almost always has a happy ending, and that’s what I’ve found in this series. Since I love </span>
  <span id="freeText11786312075943710307" style="display:none">In the past few months, I’ve developed a bit of an obsession with the television show Little House on the Prairie. It’s something I’ve seen bits and pieces of throughout my life, as there were always reruns playing on some channel. But I’ve never sat down and watched it from the beginning as I’m doing now, and I’ve really been enjoying it. I just had a desperate desire for something pure and wholesome that almost always has a happy ending, and that’s what I’ve found in this series. Since I love the television series and said series is based on a famous series of books, I obviously need to read them, right?<br /><br />This first book was absolutely adorable. Laura is five years old in this book, and still living in the Big Woods, before her family moves away. The prose is incredibly simply, and seems tailor made for reading aloud to children. There isn’t much plot, but the descriptions are vivid and very engaging, which is exactly what young children will enjoy about the book. <br /><br />I’m not a young child, so did I enjoy this book? Absolutely. I felt like I was right there with Laura, making butter and playing in an attic full of food stored for winter and listening to wolves howl outside of my window. Wilder did a great job of presenting the story through the eyes of a child, and reading it made me feel like a child again. I can’t wait to continue on with the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11786312075943710307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4320498" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4320498" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/159583-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370606661p2/159583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4320498?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/159583-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060264314" href="/book/show/1212409.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Parents and teachers as a read-aloud book, young readers of all ages</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159583-kathleen?shelf=read_aloud">read_aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159583-kathleen?shelf=early_readers">early_readers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159583-kathleen?shelf=educators">educators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/159583-kathleen?shelf=3rd-6th_independent">3rd-6th_independent</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4320498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13099230222537789021">I did a wonderful year-long read aloud with my kindergarten class last year, and it was a fantastic experience. They asked so many good questions, and it spawned so much good discussion, exciting writing and enthusiasm about the books. Kids talked, wrote and drew pictures about different episodes all year. I highly recommend it. I would have loved to integrate this with more study of one-room schoolhouses and our city so many years ago (maybe for 2nd grade?). Part of the reason this worked well </span>
  <span id="freeText13099230222537789021" style="display:none">I did a wonderful year-long read aloud with my kindergarten class last year, and it was a fantastic experience. They asked so many good questions, and it spawned so much good discussion, exciting writing and enthusiasm about the books. Kids talked, wrote and drew pictures about different episodes all year. I highly recommend it. I would have loved to integrate this with more study of one-room schoolhouses and our city so many years ago (maybe for 2nd grade?). Part of the reason this worked well for my kindergarten kids--in spite of their limited experience with Wisconsin and woods and wagons and farms--is that they, too, were only 5 or 6 years old. In imagining a little girl their own age facing such challenges and fears, and having such fun adventures, was a wonderful experience for them. Since I am a reader and reading specialist more than a kindergarten teacher, I used this book to begin a lot of wonderful deeper comprehension work. By the end of the book (and a year with other wonderful read-alouds), they were using vocabulary like "connection" and "prediction" when talking about what they thought about stories. It was invigorating and inspirational.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13099230222537789021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MSfU/7KdpEE9byAnyTVhqUBBoMRvmRpmPSPQgAlpCM0LAb0tCcNtKZpElEY+wGt2lh5HDKEUlAFmXZYxxCr6Vw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x267/QfHcZoFDm/iXPyPjWVJ/7I/9vHWucLYvrKOWT79SNIvvJm48qIl24OrCYVSsxYYevF7f7HivJ4Pf82rpA==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer9227198393555074376">Ingalls wrote a series of historical fiction books for children based on her childhood growing up in a pioneer family. She also wrote a regular newspaper column and kept a diary as an adult moving from South Dakota to Missouri, the latter of which has been published as a book.</span>
